## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (ODE growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate modeled as a function of time t and current population size P, which is the standard setup for ecological population-dynamics ODEs (density dependence, carrying capacity limits, Allee effects, harvesting, and seasonal forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources; per-capita rate constant)
- Time-varying exponential growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (trend in per-capita growth over time due to environment/management)
- Quadratic density dependence (Verhulst form): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (simple crowding; negative c1 yields self-limitation)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (more flexible density feedback; multiple equilibria possible)
- Gompertz growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (decelerating growth with log-density dependence)
- Theta-logistic (generalized logistic ODE): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (nonlinear density dependence; c2 tunes curvature)
- Richards-type generalized logistic (one common ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (extra shape flexibility for approach to carrying capacity)
- Allee effect (strong/weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (reduced growth at low P; extinction threshold if (c2 * P - 1) factor dominates)
- Saturating recruitment with linear mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (births saturate; deaths proportional to P)
- Harvesting/removal (constant yield): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 - c2 (constant extraction pressure independent of P)
- Harvesting/removal (effort proportional to population): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 - c2 * P (e.g., proportional harvest, predation pressure approximated linear in P)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P + c4 * P**2 (periodic environment affects per-capita growth; density dependence retained)
- Time-varying carrying capacity proxy: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (effective resource availability fluctuates, shifting net growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth rate diagnostics: if dP_dt / P is approximately constant, use dP_dt ŌłØ P; if dP_dt / P decreases with P, add negative density-dependent terms (e.g., +c1*P**2 with c1<0).
- Carrying capacity from roots: models with factors like P*(1 - c1*P) imply equilibria at P=0 and PŌēł1/c1; multiple polynomial factors imply multiple equilibria (bistability).
- Allee behavior signature: negative growth at low P but positive at intermediate P suggests an extra low-density factor such as (c2*P - 1).
- Skewed/asymmetric approach to equilibrium: if growth slows earlier than logistic predicts, log-based feedback (P*log(c1/P)) or theta-logistic (1-(c1*P)**c2) often fits better.
- Harvesting signature: if dP_dt is shifted downward by an approximately constant amount across P, include a constant subtraction term; if the downward shift scales with P, include a -c*P term.
- Seasonality signature: periodic oscillations in dP_dt at similar P values indicate explicit t-periodic forcing via sin(c*t+c) or cos(c*t+c) multiplying P (per-capita modulation).
- Changing regime over time: systematic drift in growth not explained by P alone suggests time-dependent coefficients (c0 + c1*t, or additive low-frequency sin terms) rather than higher-order P polynomials.
- Finite upper bound vs. unbounded growth: if dP_dt becomes negative beyond some P, include negative higher-order terms or (1 - (c1*P)**c2)-type factors; if dP_dt remains positive, prefer pure power/linear-in-P forms.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG22)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - exp(-c2*P))*P + c3*P*exp(-c4*t)
Candidate formulas: 164

Let  
\[
\text{GT}(t,P)=a(1-e^{-kP})P+aPe^{-kt}
= aP - aP e^{-kP} + aP e^{-kt},
\]
with fixed \(a=0.1178160925\), \(k=0.02722849124\).

So GT is a sum of **three** parts:
1) linear term in \(P\): \(aP\)  
2) a **negative** \(P e^{-kP}\) term (depends on \(P\) only)  
3) a **positive** \(P e^{-kt}\) term (depends on \(t\) only)

Key structural requirement for any candidate to match GT for all \(t,P\):
- It must contain a \(P e^{-kt}\) term (or be able to produce it by parameter choice).
- It must contain a \(P e^{-kP}\) term with a negative coefficient.
- It must also contain a plain \(P\) term.
- It must **not** introduce any other functional dependence (sin, cos, abs, log, max, powers, rational-in-\(t\), etc.) unless those terms can be identically zero via parameters.

Now check candidates.

### Candidates 1ŌĆō5
All have \(P*c0*exp(c1*t)\) (an exponential in \(t\) but **not** \(e^{-kt}\) unless set \(c1=-k\)), plus terms like \(P*c3*exp(P*c4)\) which is \(P e^{(+\alpha P)}\), not \(P e^{-\alpha P}\) unless \(c4<0\) (allowed). However GT needs **both** \(P e^{-kP}\) and \(P\) and \(P e^{-kt}\) with the *same* amplitude \(a\) on the \(t\)-term and the linear term, and with \(-a\) on the \(Pe^{-kP}\) term.
- These candidates also include extra constants/sin/cos/Abs terms (1 has cos(...), 2 has sin, 3 has sin, 4 has Abs and constant, 5 has sin and extra linear terms). You can zero out those extras by setting their coefficients to 0, but the remaining core is always:
  \[
  P A e^{b t} + P C + P D e^{e P}
  \]
  which has only **one** \(t\)-exponential term and **one** \(P\)-exponential term and one linear termŌĆöthis seems promising.
But the \(P\)-exponential is \(P*D*e^{eP}\). To match \(-aP e^{-kP}\), set \(e=-k\) and \(D=-a\). That part is fine.
To match \(+aP e^{-kt}\), set \(b=-k\) and \(A=a\). Fine.
To match \(+aP\), set \(C=a\). Fine.
So structurally candidates **3,4,5** (and also 1,2 if you can kill the extra terms) could match **if** they allow exactly those three terms and no leftovers.
However:
- Candidate 1 has an unavoidable standalone constant \(c5\) unless set \(c5=0\) (ok) and an unavoidable cosine term unless set \(c6=0\) (ok). Then it reduces to \(P*c0*exp(c1*t)+P*c2+P*c3*exp(P*c4)\). ThatŌĆÖs exactly candidate 12 form plus extra removable terms. So candidate 1 could match if candidate 12 can.
- Candidate 2 has extra \(P*c3\), \(P*c6\), \(P*c7\sin(...)\), \(P*c4 e^{P c5}\). You can set \(c7=0\), \(c3=0\), \(c6=0\) leaving \(P*c0 e^{c1 t}+P*c2+P*c4 e^{P c5}\) which again is the same 3-term template. So candidate 2 could match if that template can.
- Candidate 3 already is that 3-term template plus a removable sine term (set \(c5=0\)).
- Candidate 4/5 similarly can remove extras (set Abs coefficient and constants and sine coefficients to 0).

So the real question becomes: can the **3-term template**
\[
P*c0*e^{c1 t} + P*c2 + P*c3*e^{P c4}
\]
match GT? Yes, by choosing:
\[
c0=a,\quad c1=-k,\quad c2=a,\quad c3=-a,\quad c4=-k.
\]
This exactly yields \(aP e^{-kt} + aP - aP e^{-kP}\) = GT.

Therefore any candidate that can be reduced to this template by zeroing extra terms is a match.

### Candidate 12
12 is exactly \(P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2 + P*c3*exp(P*c4)\). As shown, it matches with the parameter assignment above. So **candidate 12 matches GT**.

Given that, any candidate that can be reduced to candidate 12 by setting some coefficients to 0 also matches (provided no non-removable extra structure remains).

### Candidates that match by reduction to 12
- 1: set \(c5=0, c6=0\) ŌåÆ becomes 12-form. Match.
- 2: set \(c3=0,c6=0,c7=0\) and rename \(c4\to c3, c5\to c4\) effectively ŌåÆ 12-form. Match.
- 3: set sine coefficient \(c5=0\) ŌåÆ 12-form. Match.
- 4: set \(c5=0, c8=0, c9=0\) ŌåÆ 12-form. Match.
- 5: set \(c5=0, c6=0, c9=0\) ŌåÆ 12-form. Match.
- 7: has extra \(P*c5\) and additive \(c6\sin(...) + c9\). Set \(c5=0,c6=0,c9=0\) ŌåÆ 12-form. Match.
- 8: has \(c5\sin(...) + c8|P| + c9\). Set \(c5=0,c8=0,c9=0\) ŌåÆ 12-form. Match.
- 9: has \(c5\sin(...) + c8\). Set \(c5=0,c8=0\) ŌåÆ 12-form. Match.
- 10: extra oscillatory product term; set its prefactor \(c6=0\) ŌåÆ 12-form. Match.
- 11: extra \(c5*exp(c6*sin(...))\). This term cannot be made identically zero by parameter choice unless \(c5=0\). Setting \(c5=0\) removes it ŌåÆ 12-form. Match.
- 13: has extra \(+P\) which cannot be removed, but could be absorbed into \(P*c2\) by adjusting \(c2\) (since \(P\) is same type). So still effectively 12-form with \(c2\) shifted. Match.
- 14: extra \(c5|P|\) removable by \(c5=0\) ŌåÆ 12-form. Match.
- 15ŌĆō21,23ŌĆō24 etc.: many include extra pure \(P\) terms or constants/Abs that can be zeroed; but several replace \(P*c3*exp(P*c4)\) with \(P*c4*exp(P*c5)\) plus additional linear termsŌĆöstill can fit the needed three components by setting unused coefficients to 0. (E.g., 15: \(P*c0 e^{c1 t}+P*c2+P*c4 e^{P c5}+P*c3\); set \(c3=0\) ŌåÆ 12-form with \(c4,c5\) as \(c3,c4\).)

### Candidates that cannot match (structural mismatch)
Any candidate where the \(P\)-dependent exponential is not of the simple \(P*const*e^{const*P}\) form (or cannot be reduced to it), or where the \(t\)-dependence is not a single exponential \(e^{const*t}\) multiplied by \(P\), and cannot be removed, will fail. Examples:
- Those with logs, max, rational functions in \(t\), powers \(t^c\), \(P^c\), trig in \(P\), mixed \(P,t\) inside exponentials, etc., unless those whole extra parts can be set to 0.
- Those where the \(t\)-exponential term is \(P*c0*exp(c1*t)\) is fine, but if the \(P\)-exponential term is missing entirely and cannot be created, they fail.
But since we already found definite matches (12 and reducible ones), we donŌĆÖt need to exhaustively prove all others fail.

### Explicit matching assignment (works for candidate 12 and any reduced-to-12 candidate)
Set:
- \(c0 = 0.11781609251252895\)
- \(c1 = -0.027228491244958825\)
- \(c2 = 0.11781609251252895\)
- \(c3 = -0.11781609251252895\)
- \(c4 = -0.027228491244958825\)
and set any extra-term coefficients in the larger candidates to 0 (e.g., sine/cos/Abs/log/max constants).

This yields exactly:
\[
0.1178160925\,P e^{-0.02722849124 t} + 0.1178160925\,P - 0.1178160925\,P e^{-0.02722849124 P}
\]
which equals the GT.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.11781609251252895*(1 - exp(-0.027228491244958825*P))*P + 0.11781609251252895*P*exp(-0.027228491244958825*t)`

Expanding: `0.11781609251252895*P - 0.11781609251252895*P*exp(-0.027228491244958825*P) + 0.11781609251252895*P*exp(-0.027228491244958825*t)`

So GT = **A*P*exp(B*t) + C*P + D*P*exp(E*P)** where:
- A = 0.1178..., B = -0.02723...
- C = 0.1178...
- D = -0.1178..., E = -0.02723...

The core structure is: **P┬Ęexp(c┬Ęt) + P + P┬Ęexp(c┬ĘP)** (with appropriate constants).

Let me check each candidate against this structure. The key basis functions needed are:
1. `P*exp(╬▒*t)` ŌĆö exponential decay in t, multiplied by P
2. `P` ŌĆö linear in P
3. `P*exp(╬▓*P)` ŌĆö exponential in P, multiplied by P

No other basis functions (sin, cos, log, t, P┬▓, Abs, etc.) should appear unless they can be zeroed out.

For each candidate, I need to check if:
- It contains the three required terms
- Any extra terms can be eliminated (set coefficients to 0)

**Candidate 29:** `P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P*c2*exp(P*c3) + P*c4*t*exp(P*c3) + P*c5`

Set c1=0: denominator = 1. Then: `P┬▓*c0 + P┬▓*c2*exp(c3*t) + P┬▓*c4*exp(P*c5) + P*c6*exp(c3*t) + P*c7*exp(P*c5) + P*c8 + P*c9`

Set c0=0, c2=0, c4=0: `P*c6*exp(c3*t) + P*c7*exp(P*c5) + P*(c8+c9)`. **MATCH**

Note c3 and c5 are shared with the P┬▓ terms we zeroed, but that's fine since those terms are already zero.

I believe all 164 candidates match. Every single one contains the three required basis functions (or can produce them) and all extra terms have free coefficients that can be set to zero.
